# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n",

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n",

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n",

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n",

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. Request and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing."
After
Request and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, handlers/delete.go, and handlers/patch.go. These handlers call `LogRequestObject` or `LogRequestPatch` to log the request body before processing. The patch handler specifically logs the patch bytes via `LogRequestPatch` to track what changes are being applied to resources."
